  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0bf7b8c1-2751-4e0b-bbdc-55288f8c5b31'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_188901929" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/188901929" />
    <a title="Heather Dalgarno" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5868539-heather-dalgarno"><img alt="Heather Dalgarno" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340263050p2/5868539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188901929?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather Dalgarno" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather Dalgarno" href="/user/show/5868539-heather-dalgarno">Heather Dalgarno</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5868539-heather-dalgarno?shelf=young-adult-supernatural">young-adult-supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188901929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8552156087625569917">Let me preface this review by saying that basically, this is not a good book, and I wouldn't recommend it....<br/><br/><br/><br/>The premise is that there has been a centuries long feud between two families of black magic witches in which each seeks the total destruction of the other by any means necessary. Several hundred years ago the families married their heirs - Jean and Isabeau - to try to steal each others secrets. Jean and Isabeau appear to be a sort of magically bound Romeo and Juliet. They die by betrayin</span>
  <span id="freeText8552156087625569917" style="display:none">Let me preface this review by saying that basically, this is not a good book, and I wouldn't recommend it....<br /><br /><br /><br />The premise is that there has been a centuries long feud between two families of black magic witches in which each seeks the total destruction of the other by any means necessary. Several hundred years ago the families married their heirs - Jean and Isabeau - to try to steal each others secrets. Jean and Isabeau appear to be a sort of magically bound Romeo and Juliet. They die by betraying each other and their ghosts posess their descendents in the hopes of either killing each other or being together forever, it's not entirely clear which. The main characters are from the present time, and Holly (Isabeau's descendent) having been completely unaware of her magical heritage is suddenly forced to fight for her life and the lives of her friends and family when a warlock of the rival family sets out to destroy them.<br /><br /><br /><br />The positives are that this is a good story, which jumps from the present to the past frequently to make this a sort of centuries long saga. While interesting, it is frustrating however. I am now on book 5 and still have no idea why the rival families are fighting in the first place for example. There are plot holes big enough to drive trucks through, but I am persevering in the hopes that all my questions will be answered eventually.<br /><br /><br /><br />The negatives are that this is one of the worst written books I have ever read. The characters are completely two dimensional, lacking depth and convincing motivation. The action scences are particularly poor, and read something like 'there was a bang, and a big scaly demon appeared and we all said 'oh no' and threw a fireball at it'. I'm not kidding, it's really that bad. Also, given that the main characters between them are supposed to be some of the most powerful witches/warlocks in the whole of history they seem incapable of doing any sort of useful magic. Their answer to everything seems to be to chuck a fireball at it.<br /><br /><br /><br />In the words of Magnus Magnusson, 'I've started, so I'll finish' and have moved on to the final installment. To sum up, the story is interesting, but the writing is dire. It's not a series I'll re-read, or would recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8552156087625569917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">15s</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer8458298&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8458298" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14693346116497593893">Wow. I was quite surprised how much I enjoyed these 2 books.<br/><br/>Legacy: After the rather pointless ending of the last book I was grimacing when I opened this one. Holder's problem continues to be that she fails to put in enough detail-BUT this book is more fast-paced than the others; it requires less detail on the little things so the niggling annoyances that irritate the back of your brain are less itchy.<br/>The authors show that they are perfectly capable of writing a decent story; The Golems, The Dre</span>
  <span id="freeText14693346116497593893" style="display:none">Wow. I was quite surprised how much I enjoyed these 2 books.<br /><br />Legacy: After the rather pointless ending of the last book I was grimacing when I opened this one. Holder's problem continues to be that she fails to put in enough detail-BUT this book is more fast-paced than the others; it requires less detail on the little things so the niggling annoyances that irritate the back of your brain are less itchy.<br />The authors show that they are perfectly capable of writing a decent story; The Golems, The Dreamtime and Richard finally finds his testicles, yay!<br />I felt quite compelled to read the next book, something I had not yet experienced with this series.<br /><br />Spellbound: This was gooood. They kill off the irrelevant characters: Silvana, Tante Cecile, Dan, Alonzo. <br />ITS ABOUT TIME.<br />I don't want to be callous but they deserved to die. The massive central casts of these books are one of factors dragging the series down. Good to see that Holder and Viguie recognise this and can see that these characters would never have developed.<br /><br />I loved the whole Karienne thing. A minor detail I know, but it was rather touching; their relationship always was more realistic than Holly/Jeraud. Kari's death was simple, predictable and beautiful. Her self torment throughout the series demonstrates just how inhumane Holly has become; she cares not for those who sacrifice themselves along the way. Kari is tormented by her ruthless self-analysis and her admittance of guilt makes her a likable character in the end.<br /><br />Loved to see how powerful Richard was. Ignoring how convenient it was that seven Golems turned up at the same point (I don't buy the 'thrall' theory), it was great to see him take them down with such ease. I mean the man was running and he shot a 1cm space without aiming! Not random luck. That is skill. His reunion with Nicole was heartwarming.<br /><br />Eli. Quite the little piece of shit isn't he? This is what we have been led to believe thus far. Spellbound allows the reader to see things from his perspective for the first time.<br />He still loves Nicole and risks his life to rescue her! I prefer him to Philippe. Yeh, yeh Philippe is dreamy and whatever but Eli is soo much more interesting. Plus there is the redemption factor.<br />I was stunned at how appropriate it was that he killed his father. For some reason I always thought it would be Holly or Jeraud. Loved the symmetry in JamesEli killing their fathers. <br /><br />Holly's choice. Ok I think it's fair to say that the series centres around this girl. And i'm not saying the downfall of the series was based on that. I'm not. But this book was more interesting as a result of her 'taking a back seat'.<br />When Holly is finally exorcised and the showdown begins we do expect to see some of her apocalypse-like powers. But she barely holds her own in the fight. In the end all any of them can do is summon fireballs (and raise armies of the dead-but that's just impractical). When it's all over she chooses Incest-I mean Alex over Jer. What the hell, Holly?<br />Firstly, Alex is obviously a piece of shit. <br />Secondly, what about all that soulmate stuff you've been forcefeeding us for 1200 pages?<br /><br />Is Eli Alive? Is James? Where did DemonMoore go? Who is Nicole jnr's daddy? Alex Carutherrs? Do we care about Barbara's death? Will there be a Wicked3? <br /><br />I damn well hope we get an answer to these questions and i'll be keeping an eye on her website for updates. <br /><br />The only reason I refrained from giving this 4 stars is because its predecessors are awful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14693346116497593893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_240690070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240690070" />
    <a title="Skye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6696640-skye"><img alt="Skye" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240690070?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skye" href="/user/show/6696640-skye">Skye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240690070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7316783402170012204">I read Wicked 2: Legacy and Spellbound by Nancy Holder, and Debbie Viguié. This book is one of the best book’s I’ve ever read. It’s got a lot of suspense, action, fight’s, comedy, and even some history of witches even though I don’t know if it’s real or not but I believe some of it is. They change the point of view from character to character and I love when a book does that. I liked that they had a lot of characters and I usually don’t like that but the authors made it very easy to follow. The </span>
  <span id="freeText7316783402170012204" style="display:none">I read Wicked 2: Legacy and Spellbound by Nancy Holder, and Debbie Viguié. This book is one of the best book’s I’ve ever read. It’s got a lot of suspense, action, fight’s, comedy, and even some history of witches even though I don’t know if it’s real or not but I believe some of it is. They change the point of view from character to character and I love when a book does that. I liked that they had a lot of characters and I usually don’t like that but the authors made it very easy to follow. The characters are also very interesting even the bad ones, and they describe them greatly and go very in depth with it. The only thing I didn’t like about it is that it’s a huge book because its two in one so it’s really intimidating to read it and I kind of felt like I was reading way slower than usually because of that.<br />As I said before, I really liked the way that the authors wrote. The authors didn’t use that many big words so it’s easy to understand. They not only changed the places a lot, but they also changed times. Inside the chapters they would have “mini-chapters” almost were there would be a heading saying where the person speaking was when thy were and who it was if it was present time, for example one of them was “Salem, Massachusetts: October 29, 1692.” When they do this, they go on to tell a story that ties in while the book or they continue the book when it is the main characters speaking. I’ve never heard of an author writing that way, and I think it’s really cool.<br />There are many more reasons why I love this book so much, but I just gave a few examples. I think that if I would recommend this book to anyone (which I definitely would) I would recommend it to people in high school and even most adults because it’s such an interesting book. Anyone who likes fantasy books would love this one.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7316783402170012204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The main character (whatever her name was) got so high and mighty about her connection with that old chick from old France, and how great her magic was, and "Oh, obviously this bad guy chasing my group is <i>definitely, <b>only</b></i> trying to kill me"<br /><br />Like no. <span id="freeTextContainer1919507358734639106">Since this is two books in one, I'm splitting up the review and ratings.<br/><br/><br/>Spoiler filled reviews for both books below..   <span id="freeText1919507358734639106" style="display:none">Since this is two books in one, I'm splitting up the review and ratings.<br /><br /><br />Spoiler filled reviews for both books below.. You have been warned. <br /><br />Such a long review (mainly rant).<br /><br /><br /><br />Wicked - Legacy, review, 3.8 out of 5 stars.<br /><br />Trigger warning for rape. Nothing is shown but you know it happens.<br /><br /><br />Great Kari didn’t leave after all, only to save her sorry ass. I’m glad Sasha is with Holly and her coven to go rescue Nicole and then Jer. I can’t wait for a reunion for mother and son.<br /><br />Where the hell does Kari get off blaming every single thing that happen on Holly? I know Holly has made some questionable decisions but she is young and trying to keep everyone safe. Holly did not steal Jer away from Kari like she thinks, Jer was done with Kari long before Holly even came to Seattle. If i remember correctly he was getting annoyed with her in the beginning pages of the first book. Not to mention she is basically using Sasha cause she looks like Jer and is his mom. She’s like obsessed with him when he’s clearly moved on. Don’t even get me started on the battle where Philippe’s coven and Holly’s meet. Kari abandoned Silvana, she is in her 20s, wanted so bad to know magic and bout it; but when she is in the battle she runs and abandons Silvana who is trying to fight the demons. Ugh i just really hate Kari!<br /><br />That whole little sections when Tommy confesses his feeling to Amanda was weird and kinda stupid. She finally has this realization that he’s a man now and they could be something. Then either jokes or makes a deal out of him holding her hand (i honestly couldn’t tell which) and then he just out of the blue confesses how he feels to her and that’s basically it. It switches POV. <br /><br />Holly had no right to say that Philippe didn’t care about Nicole, that he was just like the mother coven. And then…they bond?? Over wanting to attack and kill (which i think they make plans for) the Supreme Coven. Weirdest bonding session ever.<br /><br />Holly!!!! You make it so hard to stand up for you. Why did you grab Jer first and not Nicole. She is your blood!!! WTH. I feel bad for Jer he is humiliated by his appearance now which is mostly burns. Kari running out of the safehouse was stupid cause the Falcons can find her now. Silvana does’t understand that Kari was only with Jer to learn about magic for her school work! So Silvana does understand that Jer was getting tired of his relationship with Kari. Someone needs to give her a clue, so she can stop blaming everyone else. Also if Kari really loved him like she says then she would’t say or care if he looks like a monster she would love him for what is inside. Holly never once said anything about him being a monster now she loves him for him. Also it isn’t Holly’s fault that Jer was burned Amanda and Nicole pulled her from the fire. People need to lay off of Holly o know is had a bad attitude but she’s the one who has to make tough choices to protect everyone and she didn’t want any of this she was thrown into. If Sasha, Silvana, and Kari don’t like her or how she runs the coven then leave. Simple as that.<br /><br />Philippe is the only one to actually see Holly as she is and respect her. Jer needs to get over his “I’m a Deveraux. I’m cursed.” Nonsense. Why does Nicole and Philippe and Holly and Jer have to be insta love? I do not like insta love! Amanda and Tommy are the only couple that isn’t insta love but there also on the verge. <br /><br />Silvana can’t seriously be mad at Holly for not driving with her over the bridge. Silvana knee why, that she might drown or get hurt cause of the curse. So Isabeau was blocking Holly from her power so she would HAVE to sacrifice things to the goddess Hecate? I’m confused by this part I don’t know if it’s true or not. I think it is though. Isabeau is a bitch who cares for no one but herself. At least Holly came into her powers now. <br /><br />I don’t understand why Holly is so uneasy and afraid of Pablo’s gift. I know she doesn’t want him in her head but why? So he won’t see all she has done? And why does Holly think Pablo represents danger to her? <br /><br />Tante Cecile is dead?!? I thought she was unconscious! That was a fast death. <br /><br />That ending was super fast. I don’t know it everyone died or are still alive, the only ones that i know for sure are alive is Philippe, Amanda, Tommy, Holly and maybe Nicole. Speaking of Nicole why does James and Eli want her so bad? This is like the second times she’s been kidnaped by them. What tank was Michael on? I didn’t understand that part or how the house blew up. or how Amanda, Tommy, Philippe got out. I’m assuming the spear that Anne-Louise put Holly in saved her. But speaking of the Mother Coven; that was all they had to help? Basically ghosts? There not powerful like they pretend to be. And what does Michael and Laurent want with Holly? Why didn’t they just kill her? I know Michael was wanting Holly as like a mistress or something so he could use her powers but who knows. But why didn’t they call upon Pandion for help like Michael calls upon Fantasme?<br /><br />-<br /><br />Wicked - Spellbound, review, 4.5 out of 5 stars.<br /><br />Well Richard and Barbra are alive, along with Holly, Nicole, Amanda and Tommy. Ugh Kari is alive. So Armand is alive, that means Alonzo is the one Uncle Richard saw die. Silvana is dead. Yay Philippe is alive! Sasha is alive. And Dan is dead. <br /><br />Damn you go uncle Richard!!! Yay Pablo is alive I like that kid. Philippe better not be dead Pablo just better be confused about not feeling his life force or whatever. <br /><br />I love that Nicole’s cat followed her in the portal when she was kidnapped. <br /><br />If Eli really does hate his dad and James for stealing and marrying Nicole, why does he keep helping him? It makes no sense! You say you feel bad that you helped kill Jer you say you don’t trust your dad and you hate James. Why. Help. Them?!? <br /><br />Ooh damn Anne-Louise laying in to the High Prestress of the Mother Coven is everything. She only sent a fraction of them and she only sent the weakest ones! Anne-Louise is right she has no intention or interest in helping the girls defer Michael or the Supreme Coven. Someone needs to demote her and place someone else in charge of the Mother Coven. Others are questioning her too, she won’t be leader for long. <br /><br />I forgot about Jer’s body... Hopefully Dan escaped and took his body with him. <br /><br />How did Kari and Armand find Amanda and the rest? It doesn’t say! Silvana didn’t deserve to die like she did, but at least she is with her aunt now. <br /><br />The typos in this book make it hard to focus. It says Nicole’s name In the chapter but she is missing! <br /><br />I feel bad for Pablo having to find Alonzo’s grave, but I’m glad Philippe buried him. The reunion between Pablo and Philippe was sweet. <br /><br />Everyone but Dan, Holly, and Jer’s body is reunited and of course the moment is broken by the gollum’s. Poor Dan at least he is with his son and Eddie again. I’m glad the cats escaped safely but why is Amanda so sure they won’t see them again? I want Bast and Freya with them since Nicole’s cat Is with her. <br /><br />I can’t believe Michael put Holly in thrall, least of all when she is possessed by demons and then was going to rape her! Oh hell no!! <br /><br />Well Jer’s body has been found but I wonder who carries him out. There’s another Cathers witch!?!? How? I thought Holly, Amanda, and Nicole where the last ones. Who is this Carruthers and how can they help Holly?<br /><br />Great... Michael can control Holly. Wonderful 🙄. <br /><br />I need to know how a 23yo man named Alex Carruthers is related to Holly, Amanda, and Nicole and how he can help save Holly. Wow Alex is powerful is Luna admitted it. Richard is awesome!! He understood the Dreamtime better than Holly and Jer ever did. Heck he saved Jer in just a couple minutes and was able to talk to him and set up a barrier and trip alarms around him! Richard should have been a witch. <br /><br />So he’s there cousin, probably a 1st or 2nd since it never said if Holly’s dad and Marie-Claire has another brother or sister. <br />It is really specious that Alex can do all this stuff. <br /><br />I don’t trust Alex. Kari is a coward for running away and stupid for thinking she can call a truce between everyone. Did that ghost, spirit, whatever it was make Nicole pregnant? <br /><br />So not Kari had a ancestor who “dated” or mainly slept with Jean in the time of Isabeau and Jean. Not confusing at all. <br /><br />Stupid Kari!! Why in the world would she tell Michael where the coven is and about Alex and everything!! She’s betraying them!! All for the safety of Jer and most likely herself. I wonder if he did something to make her tell him. <br /><br />Why the hell would Kari drink anything Michael gave her?! And why is she feeling aroused by him. Gross Kari. <br /><br />Alex is a douche, calling Jer by his last name which he hate. I can’t believe Alex said that about killing a warlock to get his power meaning he want Jer dead. I love how Philippe and Richard are only ones who can look at Jer without flinching. <br /><br />How was Alex even able to defeat the blackfire? <br /><br />Why would they let Alex lead them even temporarily? And it just blowed up in their faces. Splitting them up to rescue Nicole and attack the Supreme Coven. He’s trying to get them killed!<br /><br />Was that Alex, Holly, Amanda, and Nicole’s cousin or a different Alex? And if it is the same Alex why does he owe her his life? Is June is mother or grandmother or something?<br /><br />Omg it was Alex he changed the timeline!! Why? What does he gain by doing that?? He saved June’s twin brothers who died in the flood. <br /><br />What the heck I’m so confused. Nicole was NOT pregnant in the last chapter! And Eli is most certainly NOT the dad! WTH it must be cause Alex messed with the timeline. But how in the hell is she almost due??<br /><br />Richard is a badass!!! Killling golems while at a dead run and throwing a knife between Eli’s legs and not hitting nothing but to just scare him. And it worked!!<br /><br />Philippe is certain that Nicole’s baby isn’t his. Why can’t it be his!! Watch it be stupid Eli. Stupid Alex rewriting time. None of this would have happened. I hope Philippe raises and is a dad to Nicole’s baby. <br /><br />Why don’t they just kill Eli? No one will miss him and Sasha will get over it. Ok who tried to kill Eli? Ugh Sasha. Why did Isabeau take Eli and Sasha? <br /><br />I can’t tell if Isa way is a bitch or a nice person.....<br /><br />How the hell did Isabeau take Eli and Sasha to 13th century France!! So Isabeau brought them there to save them. Why? <br /><br />Eli better make good with his mom since she can’t come back to the present or she will die from the ardor she took to save his worthless but. I don’t thing Sasha and Isabeau can stop the massacre. <br /><br />I still don’t get how the spell Amanda and tommy did made that portal or why. <br /><br />I understand that Jer wants his and Holly’s first time to be them and not Isabeau and Jean. But he’s so dang broody!!! I can’t stand his broodiness!! Omg. Doesn’t Jer understand they can defeat Michael if they are in thrall together!!!<br /><br />I’m loving how different Holly is since the possession. She’s better, more patient and a lot less hostile and mean. <br /><br />Barbara teaches them the best places to hit a man to take them out or kill them was funny, mainly everyone’s reactions. Especially when she said the part about their testicles.<br /><br />Seriously since when did Eli want to marry Nicole?! It’s like almost everyone is doing a complete 180! Ugh. I want to know who the dad of Nicole’s baby is. I hope it’s Philippe and he’s wrong. <br /><br />I wonder if Alex is doing this for the power he get if he kills someone since it’s Wind Moon. <br /><br />Barbara didn’t last very long did she. Kari is dead, but I’m glad she and Jer had that moment before she died. Even if I didn’t like her. <br /><br />What the.. that was the most anticlimactic death for Michael Deveraux. And I can’t tell if Sir William is alive in the demon that came from him or is dead. And I thought they had a deal why did Eli and James throw their daggers at each other? And did Eli kill James? <br /><br />This. Is. The. Worst. Possible. Time. To. Go. Into. Labor. Nicole!!!!<br /><br />There’s more Cahor witches? Is this because Alex changed the timeline by saving June’s brothers? I’m so confused with this dang timeline switch, which we still haven’t gotten anything more about. And what is Alex suggesting that they all team up and attack other covens like Michael’s. <br /><br />Is Alex seriously that he and Holly should be together together and make a coven together? Or am I reading this wrong cause she said he’s offering her something Jer can’t and won’t give her and I assume that means being together. That’s is disgusting there related!! <br /><br />What does Alex mean that Nicole’s baby is special? So Armand and Pablo are going with Alex and possibly Holly. To do more fighting. I’m with Amanda and Tommy, they fought their fight for Coventry the don’t need to fight more like Alex wants them too. <br /><br />So that’s not the real Alex that’s someone pretending to be him!!<br /></span>

I started reading a physical copy long ago, then I couldn’t continue until recently I acquired a digital copy. It’s a good story, don’t make me wrong. I will read book #5 just out of curiosity. Is like after you read the beginning you can actually predict what’s next...🙈 That bad 😐. There is so many inconclusive points of the story... I just hope the authors took that in consideration and clarify them all in the 5th book. It won’t be nice at all to keep the audience hanging like that 🙄‼️</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4130309015657253610">I read the edition with Books 3 and 4, and did a review of Legacy on it's page. I will also include it here.<br/><br/>I gave Legacy 3.5 stars. It had much more story and action than the first two, and I actually wanted to pick it up during some parts. I still have no emotional connection to any of the characters and I don't understand why its taking so long for the end battle to happen. There are so many characters! It is sometimes hard to remember who people are and all the point of view switching gets d</span>
  <span id="freeText4130309015657253610" style="display:none">I read the edition with Books 3 and 4, and did a review of Legacy on it's page. I will also include it here.<br /><br />I gave Legacy 3.5 stars. It had much more story and action than the first two, and I actually wanted to pick it up during some parts. I still have no emotional connection to any of the characters and I don't understand why its taking so long for the end battle to happen. There are so many characters! It is sometimes hard to remember who people are and all the point of view switching gets difficult to read. However, the story has more substance than the previous two. <br /><br />Book 4, Spellbound, I did actually somewhat enjoy and give it 4 stars. The action and story moved more quickly this time around. I still don't care at all about any of the characters or whether any of them live or die. There isn't really any character growth or development, maybe a little bit here and there but not enough to need to mention. I still think this all could have been shortened to two, maybe three books instead of the five that there are. This one has a pretty good cliffhanger though.<br /><br />All in all, now I'm at least a little invested in finishing the series. If I hadn't owned the books, I would have given up at the beginning. So if you can make it this far, you might as well read one more 400 page book to finish it out. Good luck.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13945293274429101361">I'm only giving the entire book a 4 star rating because Book 3 outweighed Book 4 by far. Book 3 was so compelling and I could not put it down. I loved the way all the plots finally came together only to be ripped apart again by so many twists and turns. It was exciting!! Allegiances and loyalties are defined.   <span id="freeText13945293274429101361" style="display:none">I'm only giving the entire book a 4 star rating because Book 3 outweighed Book 4 by far. Book 3 was so compelling and I could not put it down. I loved the way all the plots finally came together only to be ripped apart again by so many twists and turns. It was exciting!! Allegiances and loyalties are defined. And it turns out that the coven ends up in so much trouble that it's hard to see the light at the end of the tunnel.<br /><br />Book 4: Spellbound felt slow compared to the first 3 books. I was a little disappointed in this one. We spent so much time keeping the stories alive while everyone was separated. We as the readers already had a pretty good understanding of the past and how it affected the future and everyone in it. Then the authors took us back in the past again to change it. They threw in a new character and a new plot that I'm not sure how they can wrap it all up in the final book. The first 3 books we talk about the battle that rages between House Cahors and House Devereaux only to have it all concluded in one measly chapter. All that build up kind of felt like a let down. <br /><br />Now there is a new twist in the mix and only one book left. It makes me nervous.</span>

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer546332334&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546332334" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11575341988405625770">For this series, I'll give a quick review of it in the first volume only. This <i>Wicked</i> series is not bad, but it's not that great either. <br/><br/>One thing that I really enjoyed was the story. The plot is, as simple as I can state it, a <i>Romeo & Juliet</i> story but with families of witches and warlocks. I really like the idea of a young couple in the past not being able to move on until they kill each other. So their spirits possess a person that of their descendants (not directly) and they try to find and k</span>
  <span id="freeText11575341988405625770" style="display:none">For this series, I'll give a quick review of it in the first volume only. This <i>Wicked</i> series is not bad, but it's not that great either. <br /><br />One thing that I really enjoyed was the story. The plot is, as simple as I can state it, a <i>Romeo &amp; Juliet</i> story but with families of witches and warlocks. I really like the idea of a young couple in the past not being able to move on until they kill each other. So their spirits possess a person that of their descendants (not directly) and they try to find and kill each other.<br /><br />So Jean of the Deveraux family and Isabeau of the Cahors family married for their own gains. The Deveraux family wanted a child of Deveraux and Cahors while the Cahors wanted the secret of the Black Fire that the Deveraux had. But neither one would give the other family what they wanted and so a massacre happened and the spirits of Jean and Isabeau would not rest until they killed each other because they felt betrayed by the other. <br /><br />Now the souls of Jean and Isabeau possess the teens Jer and Holly and are trying to kill one another so they can rest. But while that's going on, Jer's father, Micheal, is trying to have Jean's father, Laurent, give him the secret of the Black Fire. <br /><br />So in this story, there are several things going on. We have a couple of flashbacks dealing with the lives of Jean and Isabeau and their families. You have Micheal and his son Eli as the villains. You have Jer and Holly trying to adapt with Jean and Isabeau possessing them while they are developing feelings for one another. And you have the rest of the characters forming allies and gathering for the very end of the battle.<br /><br />The story is fantastic and I like a story to be a little complex. But my problems are with the characters. Some of the characters.<br /><br />I really like certain characters. Jean and Isabeau are okay. Each of them have their own love and hatred for each other and it is justified and understandable. But that's more on their tragedy than on their characters. And sadly, I don't know much about them as characters. In fact, I don't even know much about their personalities. <br /><br />Their parents are awesome. Laurent and Catherine are really interesting. They are smart, resourceful, cruel, and very ruthless. They are so despicable that I found myself loving these two. I just wish we would get a little more time with them rather than the two boring love interests.<br /><br />Micheal's okay. He's a smart and powerful villain that knows what he wants and he'll do anything to get it. Eli is boring. He's just greedy and a bully and that's about it. Amanda and Nicole are really cool twin sisters. I like their differences and I really like how they are not perfect. They each have their flaws but I found them still likeable. When the book introduced Nicole, I thought that the book was going to make us hate her or have the main character hate her because of Nicole being 'sexy'. I was expecting girl-girl hatred but nope, that didn't happen and I'm glad that the book made Nicole likable. <br /><br />Jer and Holly are boring. There's nothing to say about these characters except that they just move the plot along. Jer has a little bit of character to him but that changes throughout the books. I didn't find them interesting. <br /><br />The other characters, I don't remember them. Tommy's funny and Nicole's other love interest that is introduced in book 2 is nice but I don't remember him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11575341988405625770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190357806" />
    <a title="Bryer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5758042-bryer"><img alt="Bryer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495693430p2/5758042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190357806?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bryer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bryer" href="/user/show/5758042-bryer">Bryer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781416989899" href="/book/show/8174026-wicked-2">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young Adults &amp; Adults with open minds</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5758042-bryer?shelf=ya-paranormal">ya-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5758042-bryer?shelf=own-paperback">own-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5758042-bryer?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190357806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2706376481898565214">In this one, there was a lot of new characters introduced, hidden talents of old characters blossoming, new emotions or maybe unknown emotions coming forth from everyone involved, new adorable couplings, a strong, steady and consistent concept and two really amazing, shocking and huge plot twists. At first I thought it would be a bit much, but they both blind-side you so well and mix together deliciously that it was a "perfect" twist. They weren't over bearing or obvious. They were subtle and sn</span>
  <span id="freeText2706376481898565214" style="display:none">In this one, there was a lot of new characters introduced, hidden talents of old characters blossoming, new emotions or maybe unknown emotions coming forth from everyone involved, new adorable couplings, a strong, steady and consistent concept and two really amazing, shocking and huge plot twists. At first I thought it would be a bit much, but they both blind-side you so well and mix together deliciously that it was a "perfect" twist. They weren't over bearing or obvious. They were subtle and snuck up on you, but didn't trap the reader with a desperate feeling. <br /><br />In Wicked 2 Holly FINALLY calms down, the character isn't so intense which made for an effective and powerful ending because it tapered and all the right emotions were put in place by the authors. Speaking of the authors, by the way, they are phenomenal at creating endings that create a yearning as well as a deep sense of satisfaction. These books are really like a good meal. The first few bites are sheer bliss and hit all the right notes, then after the initial draw you just start shoveling it in, hungry for more, then as it goes on you begin to tire a bit, wondering where the initial spark had gone and by the end of the wonderful meal, you feel full and reflect on the taste, craving more but feeling heavy and satisfied. Best way I can describe their writing styles.<br /><br />The fight scenes are incredible and I am glad that in this story they actually put more of a distance in between Isabeau and Jean, and Holly and Jer. The first book was great, don't get me wrong, but there was such a heavy influence from their ancestors that it really took away from the two modern day lovers which are more identifiable. The love scenes can be extremely cheesy and overdone, but the pagan influence makes it old world-y and strong, striking at the hearts of the readers. I also love that the two authors really did their homework. I absolutely love how ancient the magic and paganism felt while incorporating it with modern-day language. Perfect ladies! KEEP IT UP! <br /><br />All in all a 4.5 star read. I recommend this to anyone who has patience and a respect that not everything is flowers and rainbows because it is so hard-hitting and cruel and devilish at times. Wonderful wonderful wonderful!!!! I can't wait to get my hands on the 3rd installment to delightfully finish off the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2706376481898565214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1732249304397595503">I am actually giving this 2 1/2 stars.... This I s a story about a powerful witch that is kidnapped by a powerful warlock.   <span id="freeText1732249304397595503" style="display:none">I am actually giving this 2 1/2 stars.... This I s a story about a powerful witch that is kidnapped by a powerful warlock. He kidnaps her because he wants to use his power to control everything and everyone and he doesn't care who he hurts in the process even if it is his own sons. His son Jer happens to love Holly though so he rebels against his dad and meets up with other witches and warlocks who are trying to find Holly. <br /><br />I liked the basis of the storyline I just don't like how it was written. I liked the suspense and obstacles they ran into while looking for Holly. I also liked the monsters and demons that were around every corner that made it more difficult for them to get to Holly. <br /><br />What I didn't like about the story is there are to many characters, I could not keep them apart. Each one had there own special power. One could throw fire balls out her fingertips another one could read minds, another could make portals so you could go back in time. It was just to much to keep separate. You would read 6-8 pages as one story then another one would start. You would read another 10 pages or so then another storyline would start. Then you would be in the present time then go back in time then back to the present or somewhere in between. I just couldn't keep up with all that. At one point I think the author was even confused because she wrote about how when June was a young girl she didn't like to sleep in her room because she thought there were monsters in her closet. Her parents told her there wasn't any. Then one night she woke up to a beautiful women standing in a bright light reaching out to hold her. There was water coming out of her closet and she asked who are you and what is happening. She said I am Goddess and I am here to protect you, the dam has broke. Her parents and family died and she was left alone. Then it went to a different story line for about 8 pages or so then she wrote this same storyline again. The same exact thing except for there was a guy that was with the Godess and he said he was there to help the Goddess save her and her two brothers but her parents still died. So which is it? Was she the only survivor? Or were her brothers saved as well? I don't know because she never went back to that storyline. VERY VERY confusing!!!! <br /><br />This was a disappointing read.... Sorry</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2522741-leann?shelf=printed-book">printed-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78665103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17599498013830663461">Legacy and Spellbound are novels 3 and 4 of the Wicked series. <br/><br/>Holder and Viguie deliver again with the action and battles in the third and fourth installments in the Wicked series.<br/><br/>The war against Michael Deveraux is darker than ever in Legacy & Spellbound, and I was not disappointed with all the action. I was actually surprised, because Holly spends most of Spellbound in an altered state of mind. Spellbound really became the other characters story, and I was actually cool with it. Nicole had a </span>
  <span id="freeText17599498013830663461" style="display:none">Legacy and Spellbound are novels 3 and 4 of the Wicked series. <br /><br />Holder and Viguie deliver again with the action and battles in the third and fourth installments in the Wicked series.<br /><br />The war against Michael Deveraux is darker than ever in Legacy &amp; Spellbound, and I was not disappointed with all the action. I was actually surprised, because Holly spends most of Spellbound in an altered state of mind. Spellbound really became the other characters story, and I was actually cool with it. Nicole had a string of bad luck (and a very surprising surprise at the end), Amanda finally stepped it up a bit (and opened her eyes), and Phillippe really became an important part of the group, as did his coven members. Richard, Nicole and Amanda's father, surprised me the most. The man stepped it up big time in Spellbound, and shocked me completely.<br /><br />Spellbound left me hanging on a cliffhanger (and a few surprises at the twists in the plot), and I cannot wait to get to Resurrection.<br /><br />Highlights: Spellbound, obviously. Out of all the books, Spellbound hooked me the most. I did enjoy Legacy, but not as much as I enjoyed Spellbound. I also loved how dark this novel got, and how the characters developed yet again. Nicole and Amanda are not who they were in the first two novels.<br /><br />Lowlights: I hated how Holly was supposed to be the strongest witch, and yet she couldn't manage to save herself. In Legacy, I had my moments of boredom but they were then followed by action, so I continued on quickly. There were also some errors in the novel, but I can easily over look those.<br /><br />Also, yet again, it can be a bit confusing with a bunch of characters to remember (and a handful more that were introduced). The flashbacks made more sense to me now, though.<br /><br />Note: I may not have stated this in my review of the first two books, but I'll just say it now. I would not recommend this to anyone under 14 because of the violence, sexual references, and whatnot. If you think you're mature enough, then go ahead.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2911559371020849755">Holly has accepted her role in the feud between the covens of Cahors and Deveraux. She and Jer, who has been burned and scarred badly by the black fire have entered the dreamlands to try to save Barbara. Once there, Jer gets trapped and Holly becomes possessed. Being possessed causes massive problems among the coven members and when Michael kidnaps Holly and puts her in thrall, it seems the coven will be unable to get </span>
  <span id="freeText2911559371020849755" style="display:none">Holly has accepted her role in the feud between the covens of Cahors and Deveraux. She and Jer, who has been burned and scarred badly by the black fire have entered the dreamlands to try to save Barbara. Once there, Jer gets trapped and Holly becomes possessed. When Holly returns to her body, it's with hundreds of demons riding with her. Being possessed causes massive problems among the coven members and when Michael kidnaps Holly and puts her in thrall, it seems the coven will be unable to get her back.<br /><br />Nicole has once again been kidnapped by James Moore and finds herself a prisoner on Avalon. Even worse, Nicole is pregnant. Eli, still with feelings for Nicole decides to save her and once that decision is made, sets out to free Nicole from Avalon.<br /><br />Binding herself to Tommy, Amanda is at a loss as to how to help the remaining coven members get both Nicole and Holly back. Losing several members has taken a toll and surprisingly, it's Richard who takes an active stance. Returning to his ranger mentality that saved him in Vietnam, Richard puts his knowledge of war to work.<br /><br />Another Cahors witch has been discovered in the most unlikely of ways. Alex, a male witch who traces his ancestry back to the Cahors is approached to join the fight. Once the coven has Alex on board, he quickly takes charge. Exorsizing Holly and saving Nicole, the coven takes the fight to the Supreme Coven in London and engages in a battle that sees the death of Michael, but allows a part of William to escape.<br /><br />Once the battle is over, Holly tries once again to get Jer to join with her, but he is still resistant. Deciding to join Alex and his coven of unknown Cahors, Holly and several members of the coven set out to rid the world of evil. But, everything is not what it seems, including Alex. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mN4CfO7DVO8UIiBYy6I9+rvS+d2wKfLuIsDUePNI4wOWDBf5dCMSfHF1JnxR/ofhc7NAQt3nlZ6QEZ0gemY63w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2572874797576892732">Nancy Holder, New York Times Bestselling author of the WICKED Series, has just published CRUSADE - the first book in a new vampire series cowritten with Debbie Viguie. The last book her her Possession series is set to release in March 2011.<br/><br/>Nancy was born in Los Altos, California, and her family settled for a time in Walnut Creek. Her father, who taught at Stanford, joined the navy and the family t</span>
  <span id="freeText2572874797576892732" style="display:none">Nancy Holder, New York Times Bestselling author of the WICKED Series, has just published CRUSADE - the first book in a new vampire series cowritten with Debbie Viguie. The last book her her Possession series is set to release in March 2011.<br /><br />Nancy was born in Los Altos, California, and her family settled for a time in Walnut Creek. Her father, who taught at Stanford, joined the navy and the family traveled throughout California and lived in Japan for three years. When she was sixteen, she dropped out of high school to become a ballet dancer in Cologne, Germany, and later relocated to Frankfurt Am Main.<br /><br />Eventually she returned to California and graduated summa cum laude from the University of California at San Diego with a degree in Communications. Soon after, she began to write; her first sale was a young adult romance novel titled Teach Me to Love.<br /><br />Nancy’s work has appeared on the New York Times, USA Today, LA Times, amazon.com, LOCUS, and other bestseller lists. A four-time winner of the Bram Stoker Award from the Horror Writers Association, she has also received accolades from the American Library Association, the American Reading Association, the New York Public Library, and Romantic Times.<br /><br />She and Debbie Viguié co-authored the New York Times bestselling series Wicked for Simon and Schuster. They have continued their collaboration with the Crusade series, also for Simon and Schuster, and the Wolf Springs Chronicles for Delacorte (2011.) She is also the author of the young adult horror series Possessions for Razorbill. She has sold many novels and book projects set in the Buffy the Vampire Slayer, Angel, Saving Grace, Hellboy, and Smallville universes.<br /><br />She has sold approximately two hundred short stories and essays on writing and popular culture. Her anthology, Outsiders, co-edited with Nancy Kilpatrick, was nominated for the Bram Stoker Award in 2005.<br /><br />She teaches in the Stonecoast MFA in Creative Writing Program, offered through the University of Southern Maine. She has previously taught at UCSD and has served on the Clarion Board of Directors.<br /><br />She lives in San Diego, California, with her daughter Belle, their two Corgis, Panda and Tater; and their cats, David and Kittnen Snow. She and Belle are active in Girl Scouts and dog obedience training.<br /></span>
